After I completed for you, O sons, this book, which is the last of medical science with its completion, and I reached the end in it from its expositions and its own statements, it seemed to me fitting to complete it for you with this Treatise which is a part of operation, that is, surgery by hand.
Since operation by hand is laid low in our region and time completely lost, until perhaps the knowledge of it perished, and its trace was cut off, and there remained from it nothing except small descriptions in old books, which hands altered, and error and hesitation happened to them until its intentions were closed and its force extended: It seemed fitting to me to revive it with the ordering of this Treatise on it according to the way of exposition, declaration, and abbreviation; and to come with forms of instruments of cautery and the rest of the tools for the work; with what is done by addition from declarations and from the celerity of that which is necessary.
The reason why a good craftsman of it with his hand is not found in our time is: because the art of medicine is long, and it is necessary for its author to practice before that in the science of anatomy, as Galen narrated, until he knows the functions of the members, and their forms, and their conjunction and separation, and has knowledge of the bones, nerves, and muscles, and their number, and their emergence, and veins pulsating and quiet, and the places of their exit.
And on account of that Hippocrates said, that a name with a name is much, and with work is little, and especially in the art of the hand.
We, however, already said about that at the beginning of this book.
Since he who is not knowing what we said about anatomy, is not purged, but rather falls into error by which men are killed: just as I saw many of those who are formed from this science and boast themselves about it without knowledge, and without experiment.
This happened because I saw a stupid doctor cut open a scrofulous abscess on a woman's neck and he cut some arteries in her neck: therefore the woman's blood flowed until she fell dead between his hands.
And I saw another doctor who presumed to extract a stone from a man who had advanced in age and the stone was large. He therefore reached him and extracted it with a piece of bladder. Therefore the man died on the third day.
And I myself had already been called to extract it and I saw from the size of the stone and the condition of the sick man that he would die.
And I saw another doctor who was receiving a fee from a Duke of our land for medicine and it happened that a black eunuch who was with him suffered a fracture in his leg near his heel and the doctor rushed with his ignorance and bound the fracture over the wound with bandages and strong bindings and did not allow the wound to breathe.
Then he released him according to his wishes. Afterward he dismissed him after several days and ordered him not to loosen the bandage and it remained so until his leg and foot became abscessed and it came to destruction.
I was therefore called to him and I hurried to loosen the bandage and tranquility followed and he was freed from his pains.
However, the corruption had already been confirmed in the limb and I could not restrain it.
Therefore the corruption ceased to spread in the limb until it died.
And I saw another doctor who pierced a cancerous abscess and it became ulcerated afterward until its malice was magnified with its master.
This is because when cancer is pure from melancholic humor then it should not be reached with iron at all unless it is in a limb that can tolerate it so that its whole mass can be cut off.
And for that reason, O sons, it is necessary for you to know that an operation with the hand is divided into two divisions: namely, operation which is associated with safety; and operation, with which there is danger in many dispositions.
And I have already aroused in every place of this book, in which comes an operation, in which there is terror and fear.
Therefore it is necessary for you to beware of that, and to diminish it so that fools do not find a way to speak and dishonor.
Therefore receive measure with solicitude and protection, and your sick with ease and firmness, and use the better way leading by the grace of God to salvation and praiseworthy succession: and dismiss terrible illnesses of difficult healing: and lift up your souls from that which makes you fear so that hesitation may enter upon you in your faith and well-being.
For it is more lasting for your glory, and more sublime in this world, and finally to your quantities.
For Galen has already said in some of his admonishments. Do not treat a bad illness, lest you be named among bad doctors.
Now this Treatise has been divided according to three Chapters.
Chapter One.
On cautery with fire and cautery with sharp medicine, chaptered and ordered from head to foot, and forms of instruments and tools for cautery; and everything that is necessary in the operation.
Chapter Two.
On incision and perforation, phlebotomy and venesection, and wounds; and the extraction of arrows, and things similar to it; and all chaptered, ordered according to forms of instruments.
Chapter Three.
On restoration and dislocation, and the treatment of torsion, and things similar to it; chaptered, ordered from head to foot, and according to forms of instruments.
But before I recall the operations performed with it, it is necessary to say what are its qualities of cauteries and their harms; and in what complexion they should be exhibited.
I say therefore that speech concerning the quality of cautery's benefit and its harm is a lengthy and subtle science, and a hidden secret.
Indeed, many wise men have spoken on this subject and disagreed; and it suffices for me a little from their speeches, fearing prolixity.
Therefore I say that cautery generally confers benefit to every complexion which has matter and lacks matter, except for two complexions: a hot complexion without matter, and a dry complexion without matter.
However, in the hot and dry complexion with matter they disagreed. For some said that cautery is beneficial in it. Others said the opposite of that, namely that cautery is not suitable in a disease which arises from heat and dryness; because the nature of fire is heat; and it is inconvenient for something hot and dry to heal a disease that is hot and dry.
And he who said the opposite of that said that cautery brings benefit to every hot and dry disease which occurs in the bodies of men; because when you compare the body of man and its humors to the complexion of fire, you find the body of man cold.
And I indeed say through his speech because experience has now revealed that to me many times.
However, it is not necessary for one to come upon this unless he has already been proven and practiced in the ultimate exercise of cautery and has recognized the diversity of human complexions and the disposition of diseases within themselves and their causes and accidents, and the space of time of these things.
But there is no fear for you from the other temperaments; and especially in cold and humid illnesses. For all physicians have now agreed upon them, and they did not disagree on healing them with cautery.
And know, sons, that from the secret of healing by cautery with fire, and its goodness over cautery with burning medicine, is because fire is simple, whose action does not reach except to the member which you are cauterizing, and it does not harm another joined member with it, except for slight harm.
But the action of burning medicine reaches that which is extended from the members and perhaps causes a difficulty in healing to occur in the member, and perhaps it kills it.
But fire, on account of its subtlety and goodness of its substance, does not do that unless it overflows.
Indeed it has now become clear to us through experiment, because of the length of service and study with the art, and our standing upon the truth of things; and on account of that I excuse myself from the length of speech.
And if it were not allowed to this book of mine, I would bring to you the secret hidden in fire, and the quality of its operation in bodies by its expulsion, by which it expels illnesses with philosophical speech demonstrative, which would be fitting for your minds.
And know, sons, that they themselves disagree on the time in which it is fitting to perform cautery, and they put forward a better time for truth.
And I say that cautery is fitting in all time because the harm which happens because of time is submerged in the healing which is attracted with cautery. And especially if the cautery is for pains from necessary pains, strong ones, urgent ones, which do not tolerate delay; because it is feared from them that a greater evil may happen than a slight harm entering because of time.
And let it not enter your minds, O sons, that which the common and foolish physicians do not believe, namely that for that illness which is healed by cautery, there is not always a return; and they put this as a consequence, but the matter is not as they think; because cautery is nothing but a medicine in its place, which alters the complexion and dries up the humors which are the causes why pains occur.
However, cautery surpasses medicine in the speed of its healing, and the power of its operation, and the intensity of its dominion; and it is possible that the illness may return at some hour according to the complexion of the sick person, and the location of his illness, and its power; and what is prepared in his body from the aggregation of superfluities in it; and what comes to him in its acquisition from foods, and similar causes, unless the illness arises in which cautery is administered.
An illness subtle in a limb with few superfluities and humors, such as cautery of a tooth, on account of pain and similar things to it, for it is possible that the pain will not return there. But this happens rarely.
But truly the common saying that cautery is the last resort of medicine is a right statement: not according to what they intend in it; for they believe that there is no cure which can compare with medicine nor with any other after the cautery has been performed.
The matter is the opposite of that, and the intent in which cautery is said to be the last resort of medicine is not, except when we administer modes of treatment in some illnesses, and those medicines do not avail; then we administer cautery at the end of the matter, and it avails; then it falls that cautery is the last resort of medicine, not according to the intention which the common people and many foolish physicians understand.
The ancients said that a cautery with gold is better than a cautery with iron; and they did not say this except on account of the equality of gold, and the subtlety of its substance; and they said that it does not produce pus at the site of the cautery. But that is not absolutely true; for I have already proven it, and found that it does not do that in some bodies without others.
And a cautery with it is good, and better than with iron, as they said. However, when you ignite a cautery in fire made of gold, it is not shown to you, when ignited according to the quantity which you wish, because of the redness of the gold; and when cold quickly approaches it, and if you add fire on top of it, it melts in the fire, and turns into sheets.
Therefore, the craftsman falls from it into occupation; and because of that, a cautery with iron is made among us faster and closer, from straightforwardness to operation.
And I myself have now arranged this chapter on the cautery according to chapters; and I have arranged them from the head down to the feet, so that it may relieve one seeking that which he wants from it.
Chapter II.
This cauterization pertains to the dominion of humidity and coldness over the brain; which are two causes of headache, and a multitude of flows of humors from the head to the parts of the eyes and ears, and a multitude of sleep, and toothache, and throat pain; and universally all sickness, which happens from coldness, such as paralysis, and headache, epilepsy, and apoplexy, and similar illnesses to those.
The manner of cauterization is that you order the sick person: to evacuate in the first place with cleansing medicine three nights, or four, according to what requires the strength of the infirm person, and his age, and his habit.
Then order him to shave his head with a razor. Then make him sit between your hands on a stool, so that he has already placed his hands on his chest.
Then place the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his eyes. Wherever therefore your middle finger arrives, mark that place with a cautery.
Then with an olive-wood cautery: which has this shape.
Then place it on the spot marked with the cautery, descending in such a way that your hand constricts gradually, and you revolve it. Then lift your hand quickly and look at the place.
And if you see that a quantity equal to the head of an alky or a quantity equal to rue has already been exposed from the bone, then lift your hand. And if not, repeat your hand with the iron itself, or with another from it if it becomes cold: until the bones which I told you are seen.
Then take some salt and dissolve it in water, and soak the cotton wool in it, and place it on the spot; and leave it for three days.
Then place cotton wool soaked in butter on top of it, and leave it on the spot until the burn is destroyed. Then care for it with tetrapharmakon ointment until it is healed.
It has been said that the more a wound remains open, the more pus it emits: therefore it is better and more beneficial.
And some of them have said that the skin should be cauterized up to the bone, and the cautery should be held until something of the thickness of a bone is charred.
Then after that which has been charred is scraped off from the bone, then it is cared for.
And others say that it is necessary with the cautery to reach the very end until it imprints a template on the bone so that the bone falls away, which is done like the shape of a kirate: or an instrument which women put in infused with a small alphabet; and they believe that vapors from the head are exhaled from this place and the wound is left open for a long time.
Then it should be cared for until it is consolidated.
But these two kinds of cautery do not seem to me to be anything other than according to the way of fear in certain men.
And to dismiss him, is better with his health according to me.
For the head is weakened from the solution of its natural continuity, as we have testified in other members; and especially when the head of a weak, feeble person is; and the first kind of cautery is indeed safer and better for me, and I use it; therefore operate with it safely.
Chapter III.
When a chronic pain occurs in the whole head and it is prolonged in a weak person, and they use leeches, poultices, head-purgatives, oils, and emplasters. And especially if it has already been cauterized with one cautery, which we have described, and those things do not bring him any relief, then consider. For if the head of a weak person is strong by nature and is not feeble, and it encounters severe cold, then cauterize with another cautery under that one a little. Then cauterize it over the whole horn of its head with a cautery, so that it does not pass through the skin, and uncover from the bone a quantity, as we have described. And cauterize it with one cautery on the back of its head, in the place which is called "vas"; and this place is where the wind is placed; elevate your hand in this, and do not uncover the bone. For the weak person finds because of that severe pain, and different from the pain of all other head cauteries.
And I say this cautery in its place; and it is necessary that it be a cautery with which the horns of the head are cauterized, and the back of the head with a more subtle cautery, with which the middle of the head is cauterized.
Chapter IV.
When pain and swelling occur in a part of the head, or the pain extends to the eye, and the head is purged with purifying medicines, and the remaining treatment, which I mentioned in the divisions of diseases, is administered, and it does not fully resolve; then cauterization is appropriate in this case according to two methods: either cauterization with a sharp, burning medicine; or with iron.
Cauterization with a sharp, burning medicine is done as follows: take one clove of garlic and peel it, and cut off its ends from both sides. Then split the place of pain at a time when bloodletting is broad, until a place under the skin is made where the tooth is taken.
Therefore insert it just under the skin until it is concealed; then bind it above with a constriction appropriate for a poultice, and leave it for fifteen hours; then loosen it and remove the garlic; and let it rest for two or three days; afterwards apply a swab dipped in butter over it until the place forms pus; then treat it with ointment until it is healed.
And if you wish to do so with certain burning medicines, which I wrote in the twelfth treatise, On Burning Medicines.
Cauterization of it with iron is done as follows. Heat the cautery, whose shape is this.
And it is called a cautery iron because the shape of its head is like the shape of a key, which has some curvature and in the middle of it there is a small prominence.
Then place it upon the location and hold your hand steady; and turn the iron gradually with speed; and the amount that is cauterized should be half of the thickness of the skin. And raise your hand so that the artery which is below is not injured and bleeding may occur.
Then soak a compress in salt water and place it on the spot and leave it for three days; then place the compress with butter; afterwards treat with ointment until it is healed.
And if you wish, cauterize this hemi cranium with the second point of the cautery. And beware of cutting an artery in this hemi cranium, not an old one properly.
Concerning the method of cauterizing an old hemi cranium.
When you treat a hemi cranium with what we said from the previous treatment and what we said in the divisions of diseases and the treatment does not work; and you see from the illness that it is not sufficient for it what we said from the first cautery with medicine, or with cautery with fire, then it is necessary that you ignite the knife cautery until it becomes white after you mark a line on the spot of pain whose length is half a finger, or so; and place your hand with one finger, and press it until you strike the artery and reach up to the mouth.
However it is necessary for you to be careful of the continuation of the mandible, which moves during chewing, lest its side or the nerve that moves it be injured, from which a spasm may occur.
And be watchful and careful about the flow of blood from the artery which has been cut. For in its cutting off there is fear, and especially for him who does not know that which he is doing, and is neither studious nor experienced; and he abandons the operation with it at first.
And I will come with a recollection of the regimen of the flow of blood occurring from an artery according to its manner, and in its place in this book.
If you see from the illness that this cautery is not sufficient for it, and you see the body of the weak person enduring the cautery in the middle of the head, as we have described, care for the wound until it heals.
And if you wish, apply the cautery that we mentioned in the chapter on the extraction of an artery with a cautery having two knives. For this cauterization is better and more effective.
On the manner of cauterizing for ear pain.
When pain occurs in the ear from cold and is treated with solutions and the remaining treatment as we have mentioned in the division, and the pain is not removed, then apply a cautery by fire. And this is what is called a Point, its shape is as follows.
Then points with it after its ignition are made in a circle around the entire ear, as it revolves; or in a circle around both, if there is pain in both at the same time. And distance yourself with the cautery from the root of the ear a little, after you have marked the places with an ointment; and let the quantity of the cautery be ten punctures in each ear, and like that.
Then care for the places until they heal.
On the manner of cauterizing for a sprain.
Chapter Seven.
A sprain that is treated with cautery is only of the types that occur from phlegm, according to what we have said in the divisions of illnesses.
And avoid cautery for types that occur from dryness and nerve spasm.
When you treat this type of sprain with herbs, poultices, and gargles, and your treatment does not take effect, then it is necessary that you cauterize the patient with three cauteries: one at the root of the ear, the second a little below its temple, and the third at the junction of the two lips.
And place your cautery opposite the weak part. For softening does not happen unless in the part which appears healthy.
And the form of cauterization is, to cauterize it with the cautery itself in a straight line from the upper extremity of the ear below the horn of the head a little; and at another time: whose length is according to the length of the thumb. And place your hand with the cautery until a quantity of half the thickness of the skin is burned.
And this is the form of the cautery, and it is a kind from the one with a blade, whose form was mentioned before; however it is not thinner by a little, as you see; and it should be that the knife in it has unnecessary thickness a little.
Then care for the places, with what preceded, until they are healed.
On the manner of cauterizing in old apoplexy.
When apoplexy becomes old, and you care for it with what we said, and your medication does not help, and the weak person does not have a fever, then cauterize him with four cauteries above all the horn of his head, and with a cautery in the middle of the head, as we said, and with a cautery on the back of the head, according to what preceded; and let the manner of the cautery be according to what preceded.
Also cauterize with a cautery above the mouth of the stomach: and it is more final.
Then care for it, with what preceded.
Chapter Nine.
It is necessary that first the weak person be given a large quantity of hyssop and pills that purify the brain.
Then shave the head of the weak person completely and place on the back of his head a plaster of sycamore as described in the treatise on plasters; and apply it several times.
Indeed, this is the method of cautery; and do that in the same order as I said there.
Therefore if it heals thereby, it is good. If not, then do three cauteries on the back of his head, which descend from the upper part of the head to the lower part of the eye; and put the breadth of a finger between each cautery.
Then care for the cautery, as with the one that preceded it.
But if you wish an addition, and he is able to tolerate it; then do a cautery for him in the middle. And if you wish an addition, then cauterize him above the two horns.
Then care for him until he is healed; and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to the form that was mentioned previously.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in paralysis and softening.
Chapter Ten.
It is necessary that you proceed with the purification of the head with hyssop and with what we have said.
Then shave the head of the sick person; afterwards cauterize him with a cautery in the middle of the head, and with a cautery above each horn of the head, and with a cautery above the back of it, and with three above the vertebrae of the neck.
But if you are dealing with illness in softening of the body with more than those, and he is able to tolerate it, and the illness is strong; then cautery him with four cauteries above the vertebrae of the back, and the last one with a cautery until most of it is burned from the skin, and raise your hand. Then care for him until he is healed; and thus let the cautery be olive-shaped.
Concerning the method of cauterying in epilepsy.
An epileptic is not cauterized unless his epilepsy is from phlegm.
Therefore it is necessary that you cleanse his brain first of all with vinegar, and with the remaining treatment which we mentioned in the division: when he is strong, or when he can bear taking medicines.
But if he is a child who cannot bear medicines, then a gargle and cleaning mastications for the brain are given before it, for many days with good food.
Then shave his head, and afterwards cauterize it with one cautery in the middle of the head, according to what preceded in the manner; and with another cautery on the back of his head, and with a cautery over all the horn of his head. But if the sick person is strong and can bear it, then cauterize him with the cauteries which I mentioned in the one having paralysis, and softening of the body over the vertebrae of the neck and the vertebrae of the back; and let the cautery be olive-oil according to the manner which preceded.
But if the sick person is a child then put a delicate cautery according to this manner.
Concerning the Manner of Cauterizing in Melancholy.
When the causes of melancholy are corrupted humors and thick phlegm, then cauterize him with the cauteries which we mentioned in the one having paralysis.
And if the cause of melancholy is a superfluity tending towards melancholy and the body of the sick person is damp, then give him a drink which will cleanse his brain, according to what preceded in the division; then shave the head of the sick person, and afterwards make a well-shaped turband out of linen, like a circle.
Then place it in the middle of his head; and the sick person sitting straight should be held on all sides.
Then present a liniment. And it is more fitting to be made from old butter. And heat it over a fire with a tempered heat, which the finger can bear when introduced into it. Then evacuate it in the middle of his head in a circle, and let it alone until it becomes cold.
Do that to the weak one once a week, with the rest of his good regimen, until he is healed.
Or if you wish, cauterize it by making many small punctures on it, except where you hold it with the cautery: let there be a smell.
For this kind of cautery moistens the brain with quality.
Then put a swab soaked in butter or chicken fat on top of it.
On the manner of cauterizing descending to the eye in water.
Chapter Thirteen.
When the beginning of water in the eye is declared to you by the signs which I have said in the division, then begin and make the weak one drink, with that which cleanses his head.
And keep him from all moistures, and have him sit in a bath, fasting for several days.
Then instruct him to shave his head, and cauterize it in the middle of his own head. Then cauterize it above the two temples with two cauteries, if there is a beginning of the descent of water in both eyes at the same time; or from one side, if there is a beginning of water in one eye; and cut off with the cautery all the veins and arteries which are under the skin; and let the cautery be long in width above the temples; and beware of the flow of blood.
For if you see anything from it, then cut it off immediately with whatever medicine is possible; and I will come with the wisdom which is in the extraction of arteries and the cutting off of them and caution from the flow of blood.
And sometimes it is cauterized on the neck, under the two bones, with two cauteries lastly produced.
On the manner of cauterizing old tears.
When tears of the eyes are old, persistent, and are upon the veins and arteries which are on the outer surface of the head, it is verified that this is from cold, phlegmatic superfluities; then cauterize with the same cautery as I have described in the beginning of descending water, with a cautery in the middle of the head, and two cauteries upon two temples, and two cauteries on the neck under two bones. And if it does not yield with addition, then cauterize it on every side cautiously above the eye, upon the extremity of the eyebrow with a small cautery.
Concerning the method of cauterizing for a foul smell of the nose.
When you treat it with that which we said in the division, and medication does not avail, then hasten and give in a draught three nights of infirmocochias; then shave its head and cauterize it with a medium cautery, with an olive-wood cautery. Then cauterize it with a small cautery, with two cauteries on the two eyebrows a little under the hairs.
And guard against the artery so as not to strike it.
And this is the form of a small cautery.
Concerning the method of cauterizing for relaxation of the eyelid.
When the eyelid of the eye becomes relaxed from illness or moisture, then cauterize the eyelid with one cautery, with a moon-shaped cautery.
And if you wish, cauterize it above the two eyebrows a little with two cauteries on every side; and let them be extended from the two temples; and let the length of the whole cautery be according to the lengths of the eyebrow; and do not finish your hand with the cautery, but rather according to the amount that the third eyelid is burned.
On the way of cauterizing an eyelid when prickly hairs are turned inwards and irritate the eye.
A cautery is of two types: either a cautery with fire or a cautery with a burning medicine.
However, in a fire cautery, advise the patient beforehand to let their hairs grow out, if they are among those who remove them, until they are lengthened and even. But if they sting him at their root, then bind his eyes with a strip so that they do not move until they are born.
Therefore, when they are born and even, then place the patient's head in your lap; then mark on the eyelid of his eyes with wax, a mark that is according to the shape of a myrtle leaf; and let the beginning of the mark be near the hairs.
Then place cotton soaked in albumin or in psyllium mucilage over the eye.
Then with fire a cautery, whose shape is this.
Then cauterize over the shape which you have marked gradually in many times until the surface of the skin which is like the shape of a myrtle leaf, is entirely burned properly.
And the sign of the success of your work is: that if you see the eyelid of the eye already contracting and the hairs rising at the puncture of the eye.
Therefore, raise your hand then, and let him go for three days.
Then place cotton with butter on it until the eschar is eradicated. Then care for him with ointment until he is healed.
And if any hair returns after an hour and the eyelid softens, then repeat the cautery over that place as you did at first.
If, however, the hairs are on the lower eyelid, then cauterize it until it is raised to its natural place; and make it even so that the hairs do not prick the eye.
It is as if you should direct the sick person to let the hairs grow out until they are lengthened and even. Make from paper or cloth a shape of a myrtle leaf.
Then take from known soap and from lime not imbibed from each one weight of one ounce or nearly that; then grind them together with good attrition and make it quickly so that it does not become cold. Then from the pan spread it upon the paper which you have made like a myrtle leaf shape and place it upon the eyelid of one or both eyes. And place under the eye a piece of cloth soaked in albuminous fluid; and let the head of the sick person be in your lap.
And place your index finger upon the medicine and press it for a short time. And you will move it whenever the sick person feels the bite of the medicine; because it finds its bite like fire.
While therefore he perseveres in this, that he finds the bite, then let go of the medicine and move it with your finger. When therefore the bite quiets, then remove the medicine and wash the eye with water.
And consider then if you see the eyelid being raised as it is raised with fire or incision, it is well; and if not, then repeat upon it from the medicine upon the place where the medicine does not imprint and does not stain until your operation is equal and the eye contracts.
Then place upon it a cloth with butter until the skin burn is eradicated. Then care for it with diaphinicon ointment or another until it heals.
And it is necessary for you during surgery, that you guard with the utmost care, lest anything from the medicine should fall into the eye.
If the eyelid softens after a few days and something from the hairs fights its way into the eye, then repeat the medicine upon that place which softens from the eyelid itself, just as you did at first. Then take care of it until it heals.
And this is the form of a myrtle leaf.
And know that the eyes of men are diversified in size and equality. Therefore let your consideration be according to that, and the way of righteousness is not hidden from him who has a desire concerning this art.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in lacrimal fistula.
When you heal a fistula, as we said in the divisions of diseases, and your treatment does not work: then it is necessary that you cauterize it according to this method.
Instruct the sick person to put his head in your lap, and let a servant hold his head between his hands in such a way that it does not move or shake with his head.
Then put a cotton swab soaked in egg white or in psyllium mucilage over his eye; then with fire a cautery, whose form is this.
Let it be concave, like the shape of a vultureâ€™s quill pen from one end, with which the cautery is made; and if you wish for it to penetrate all the way to the other end, and if you wish for it to go upward, then try thus.
However this concave shape is better for your purpose.
Then press out the fistula if it is open and extract the pus from it and dry it out; and if it is not open, then open it and extract its pus.
Then place the cautery upon it, which has been heated intensely.
And hold your hand with it a little while by the cautery from the eye, to the side of the nose, so that your hand does not stray, or the weak one is not disturbed: and you place the cautery in the fat of the eye, and corrupt it.
So if you reach in the beginning of your cautery up to the mouth, it will be well. And if not: then repeat the cautery once, or twice, if it is necessary with it: and dismiss it for three days.
Then place cotton with butter, and care for it with a drying ointment until it is healed.
And if forty days pass it and it does not heal: then place upon it a sharp corrosive medicine until the mouth is uncovered: and scrape it according to what comes in its chapter.
And there is another method of cautery for fistula, which some first said. Attend to the place of the fistula, and find it: then put a thin camahan into the fissure, that is, a thin cannula, whose shape is this. And pour into it a quantity of a drachma from melted lead, and hold your hand with the cannula in good retention, and do not move the weak one at all so that the melted lead does not run or reach its eye.
And it is necessary that you place cotton infused in albumin, yes, or in water upon the eye of the weak one.
For lead burns the place of the fistula, and heals it with a marvelous healing.
If the fistula is healed with what we said from cautery and care, it is good. And if not, then it is necessary to administer a nostril, and reduce the fistula to the course of the nose, according to what will come in its own place.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in fissures of the lips.
Very often there occur in the lip fissures which are called harelips, and especially in the lips of infants.
Therefore when you treat these fissures, as we said in the division of diseases, and the treatment does not help, then a small heated knife cautery, according to this form.
And let its concavity be according to the subtlety of the knife.
Then place the heated cautery quickly in the fissures themselves until the cautery reaches the depth of the fissures.
Then care for it with cerate until it heals.
On the manner of cauterizing a fistula of the mouth.
When an abscess occurs in the root of the gum, or in the palate, or in the roots of the teeth: then it makes pus and bursts: afterwards it becomes chronic and discharges pus and a fistula forms: then you treat it and the treatment does not help, then it is necessary to apply a heated cautery according to the size which will fit into the fistula. Then insert the heated iron into the opening of the fistula and hold your hand until the heated iron reaches its depth and end: do this once or twice.
Then care for it afterwards with what we said about care until it is healed.
If therefore the discharge is cut off and it heals, it will be good. And if not, then it is necessary to uncover the place and remove the corrupt bone according to what will come in its chapter.
On the manner of cauterizing the gums and softened teeth.
When the gum softens because of moisture and the teeth are loosened and you treat it with medication and it does not help: then place the head of the weak person in your lap.
Then a cautery by fire, whose form will come after this, so that you put the Cannula over the tooth; and insert into it the ignited Cautery quickly: and hold your hand for a short time, until the weak one feels the heat of the fire has now reached the root of the tooth.
Then raise your hand; then repeat the Cautery several times, according as you wish.
Then let the weak one fill his mouth with salt water, and hold it for one hour; and spit it out.
For the tooth moved is made firm, and the softened gum is tightened, and the corrupted moisture is dried.
Concerning the way of cauterizing in Toothache.
When the pain of a tooth is because of coldness, or there is cold itself in it, or a worm, and treatment with medicines does not help; then the Cautery is upon it according to two ways: either Cautery with butter; or cautery with fire.
But the Cautery of it with butter is, so that you take vaccinated butter, and boil it in an iron spoon, or in a crucible. Then take cotton, and wrap it over the end of the tentacle. Then dip it into the boiling butter; and put it on the painful tooth quickly, and hold it until it cools; then repeat it several times, until the power of the fire reaches the root of the tooth.
And if you wish, dip wool, or cotton in cold butter, and put it on the aching tooth; and put ignited iron on top of it, until the fire reaches the depth of the cavity of the tooth.
But cautery with fire is, so that you apply to a cannula of air, or a cannula of iron. And let there be something of thickness in its body, so that the sharpness of the fire does not reach the mouth of the weak one.
Then apply a cautery iron, the shape of which will be shown; and place it upon that tooth; and hold your hand there until the cautery iron cools.
Repeat this several times, for the pain will be removed, either on the same day or another day.
And it is necessary that after the impression of the cautery iron, the sick person should fill his mouth with good butter and hold it for one hour; then spit it out.
And this is the shape of the cautery iron.
Cauterize with whichever extremity you wish, as is possible; and this is the shape of the cannula.
On the method of cauterizing fistulas.
When fistulas are from phlegm and cold humors, and are not obedient to digestion by medicines, and you wish to hasten their digestion; then apply a concave cautery iron, the shape of which is this.
Having two open extremities so that the smoke may escape from the cautery iron at one extremity; and place it ignited upon the abscess once, and a second time if needed, until it reaches the depth of the abscess.
But if the abscess is small, then place the cautery iron according to the size of the abscess.
Then leave it for three days, and place a poultice soaked in butter upon it until what was burned by the fire is removed.
Then treat it with tooth ointment until the shape of the cannula is healed.
On the method of cauterizing hoarseness of voice and constriction of breathing.
When humors overcome the bronchial tubes, and especially when this is accompanied by coldness of complexion, then it is necessary that the sick person first be evacuated with dissolving medicines.
Then cauterize it at night near the root of the throat in a depressed place, and beware that you do not reach the throat with the cautery, nor the skin except for a little bit of it.
Then cauterize it with another cautery at the junction of the neck on the last vertebra, ending it. And let the cautery be small according to the previous way.
Then treat it with what precedes until it is healed.
On the method of cauterizing in illnesses of the lung and cough.
When a cough and lung ailment are from cold humors, and the weak person does not have a fever nor phthisis, and the ailment is old: then cauterize him with two cauteries above the collarbone in depressed, smooth, empty places. And with another cautery in the middle of the chest between the two nipples: and let the cautery be like a cannula according to the previous form.
And if you wish your cautery to be by pricking with a cautery which is called a Point, whose form preceded in the cauterization of ear pain: and let there be points from thirty points up to others.
Then treat him with what precedes until he is healed.
And now let the cautery have three branches according to this form. Therefore cauterization is relieved when you do it with that juice along with three cauteries.
Chapter Twenty-Seven.
When the head of the humerus is dislocated due to humors, and it does not stay fixed within an hour of its return from its dislocation until a habit of returning is established, then afterwards it is dislocated by a slight movement, which happens as we have already testified: then it is necessary for you to first reduce the dislocation. Then the weak person is laid on his back, or on his sound side. Then raise the skin which is inside the nipple upwards with your left hand's fingers and if the joint dislocates inwards.
Then having a cautery with two points of fire. Whose shape is this.
Then cauterize the skin until it penetrates to the other side and there will come a cauterization figure with four cauteries.
And sometimes the cauterization is done with a cautery having three points, therefore the figure of the cauterization then is of six cauteries and the points are tested according to subtlety.
And this is the shape of a cautery having three points.
And sometimes one more is added in this manner so there are eight cauteries.
Then place on the cautery pounded leeks with salt. Then make the weak person adhere to quiet so that the limb is not moved for a time until it is strengthened.
And if the dislocation is upwards, and this rarely happens, then cauterize it on the shoulder with a clavicle cautery, or by puncturing with many cauteries.
For the joint is strengthened and the humidity is removed and the weak person is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the stomach.
When cold and much humidity happen in the stomach until they draw it away from its complexion and multiply catarrh to it and constant modes of treatment and do not help then it is necessary that the weak person be laid on his back and extend his legs and arms. Then cauterize with three cauteries, a cautery under the breastbone the size of one finger with a clavicle cautery, and two cauteries below from both sides of the one cautery until there comes a triangular figure of cauteries. And lengthen between each so they do not join together when they form pus.
And let the depth of the cautery be the amount of two-thirds the thickness of the skin.
And let the shape of the cauteries be according to this form without addition: and if you wish, cauterize with a large cautery in the middle of the stomach according to this form: and let the cautery with which this cautery is made be one according to the shape of a circle according to this form.
And the stomach is cauterized by pricking it for one who is afraid of this cautery: and it is, that you sign on the stomach a point according to the amount which you wish with an encaustic: then cauterize it itself with a point cautery: then care for it with the care which preceded until it heals.
Concerning the way of cauterizing a cold epar.
When it happens in the epar that pain arises from coldness and humidity, or from thick windiness until superfluous egress departs from its own natural complexion, and the infirm is cured with what we said, and does not progress in it: then it is necessary that the infirm be laid on their back on their neck, and signs with an encaustic three cauteries according to this form, and this same quantity above the epar below the hypochondria where the elbow of a man reaches: and let the space which is between each cautery be according to the thickness of a finger: and let the cautery be according to the length of the body straight: and do not compress your hand much with the cautery.
And let the quantity of what is burned from the thickness of the skin be the quantity of half of it not added to: and let the infirm person stand on their own feet.
But if he is not standing, then let him lie down, who has already extended his legs and raised his arms.
This is the form of a cautery.
And it is indeed possible for you to cauterize with this cautery using a knife cautery when you have subtlety and prudence in the art.
And guard yourself, so that you do not proceed too far in cauterization and the thickness of all the skin is hardened, therefore the whole body is hardened and it reaches the intestines; for the skin there is subtle, know therefore that.
On the method of cauterizing liver abscesses.
When it happens that you wish to know if the abscess is in the flesh of the liver or in its tunic: then if it is in the flesh of the liver, a weak pain and heaviness occur without sharpness; and if it is in the tunic of the liver, there is sharp vehemence with pain; and you see now that his treatment has wearied his doctors.
Therefore it is necessary for the sick person to lie on his neck. Then mark the place of the abscess with wax; then heat a cautery which resembles a ray. And this is its form. And cauterize with it one time until all the skin is burned and it reaches the underlying tissue, until all the pus comes out; then treat it with treatment for ulcers until it is healed.
And it is not necessary to use this species of cautery except by one whose study in the medical art is prolonged and through whose hands these kinds of illnesses concur many times with experiment; then let him dare to perform this type of operation.
But truly it is better for me to leave it.
On the method of cauterizing pleurisy.
The ancients said to cauterize cold pleurisy with a cautery using the roots of birthwort in this way. Take one longer root from the dried long roots of aristolochia, and let it be as thick as a finger. Then immerse it in oil and ignite it in fire. Then cauterize with one cautery in that which is between the continuation of the collarbone and the neck, and with two small cauteries a little below the guidezi towards the part under the beard.
And with two cauteries also in that which is between the fifth and sixth rib a little below towards the back; and with another cautery in the middle of the chest, and another above the stomach. And with three cauteries from behind: one in that which is between the two shoulder blades; and with two cauteries from the two sides of the chest, below the cautery which is between the two shoulder blades.
And it is not necessary to compress your hand with the cautery, rather let it be evident on the skin by smelling.
And certain ancients have said that there are men who use a cautery of iron similar to a spoke; they ignite it and insert it into that which is between the ribs until they reach the abscess with it, and pus flows out as we said in the abscess of the liver.
But in this perforation with a cautery there is fear, that either the weak one dies immediately, or a fistula occurs in the place, for which there is no healing.
Concerning the way of cauterizing the Spleen Chapter Thirty-Two.
When you treat a spleen ailment, as we said in the treatment of divisions of diseases and your treatment does not work, then there is a cautery for it according to three methods, all of which are correct.
One of which is to make three or four cauteries in a line according to the length of the spleen according to the figure of liver cauteries, the figure of which precedes.
And let there be between every cautery a quantity of the thickness of a finger, or more or less.
And let the method of cautery, which we have said in cautery of the liver be equally.
And do not press your hand with the cautery: and let the weak patient be supine on his back.
And another method of cauterization is: to have the cautery with two true points of fire, as we said in the chapter of shoulder dislocation: and elevate the skin which is directly over the spleen where the left elbow of the weak patient reaches: and let your elevation be such that you elevate the skin according to the width of the body so that the cauteries may fall according to the length of the body.
Then introduce the two points ignited deeply, until with them you penetrate the skin on the other side: then withdraw the cautery: thus there are made four cauteries.
And if you wish, cauterize with another cautery having three points.
Then care for the cautery after you have dismissed it to discharge pus for many days: for it is more bringing together than any other which preceded from the cure.
On the method of cauterizing in dropsy.
A cautery does not fall in dropsy unless on the legs properly.
When you treat a dropsy with the methods of cure which we have said in the division, and the cure does not bring together then it is necessary that you cauterize it with four cauteries around the navel, and one cautery over the stomach, and another cautery over the liver, and one over the spleen, and two cauteries down the back between the vertebrae, and one directly on the chest, and another directly on the stomach: and let the quantity of depth of the cautery be near the thickness of the skin.
Then dismiss the cautery open so that it discharges pus for a long time.
And do not withhold the weak from treatment after cautery with him, for it is necessary that two intentions be brought together for him, and healing will hasten to him with the help of God.
But the form of the cautery with which the abdomen is cauterized should be clauilis, according to its previous form; and that with which the back is cauterized should be olive-shaped, according to its previous form.
Concerning the manner of cauterizing feet and legs.
When abscesses form in dropsy and are filled with clear water, you must cauterize on the back of the foot at the nocrati, which is between the auricular and annular bones; and raise your hand with the cautery, and do not twist it; then raise your hand and do not rub it at all.
For the clear water will redden, and the cautery should be of this form.
Then make two cauterizations on each leg, and let the cautery be made with the blade end of the cautery; and let the cauterization be made according to the length of the leg, one below the knee and the other below it, about the middle of the leg; and make two cauterizations on each thigh; and leave the cautery open without treatment for a long time so that some water may redden from it; then treat it with the rest as we have said.
Concerning the manner of cauterizing in the resolution of the abdomen.
Chapter Thirty-Five.
When there is a resolution of the abdomen from cold and moisture until the retentive and digestive powers which are in the stomach and intestines are weakened, and it is treated with modes of treatment and does not heal, and you see the sick person tolerating a cautery of abundant power, then cauterize him with a large cautery over his stomach, according to what preceded in the cauterization of the stomach with a circular cautery; and four slender cauteries in the circumference of the umbilicus, with a slender clauilis cautery; and a cautery above the groin above the ilium with a large one or two.
And if you see abundant moistures and a weak patient enduring it, then cauterize it with a cautery over the comb, and with a cautery over the whole groin; and perhaps you will add two small cauteries on the abdomen near the large one.
For it is a beneficial cure, whose benefit does not stray.
Concerning the Method of Cauterizing Hemorrhoids.
Chapter Thirty-Six.
When there are many old hemorrhoids or one in the anus, and they are from thick, cold humors, or corrupted humidities, and they are cured with what we said in the division, and the cure does not avail; then cauterize with three cauteries on the lower lumbar vertebra under the armpit a little triangularly, and with a cautery under the navel as if with two fingers.
And if you think that his stomach is chilled and his food is not digested, and you see his face inflamed, then cauterize him on the stomach with a large cautery, according to what preceded; and with a cautery over his liver, and another over his spleen with a clauile cautery; and leave the cautery open for a time: then care for him until he is healed.
Chapter Thirty-Seven.
When you excise atherlomas, then heat a cautery that resembles a rod. Then insert the ignited one into the excised atherloma; and with your last hand until it reaches the orifice of the vein from which blood runs; do that once or twice.
If therefore there are many atherlomas, then cauterize each one with a cautery according to what we have described. Then care for them with what is beneficial to them from ointments, until they are healed.
And if you cauterize it with a large cautery over the alcatin, it is more final for healing.
On the Manner of Cauterizing a Fistula in the Anus.
Chapter Thirty-Eight.
When the sick person does not submit to incision and the work which we have described in its place, and is terrified by it, perhaps he is healed with a cautery.
Therefore when it happens to someone that a fistula has become old, and pus runs from it, and corrupt humors. It is therefore more fitting that which is necessary, so that you should test it with a delicate probe. Then recognize the depth of it with the probe.
Then ignite a cautery which is similar to a spoke. Then insert yourself ignited into the fistula and the quantity into which the peg entered.
And repeat the cautery over it until all those corrupt bodies are burned, once, or twice, or three times, according to the quantity of your need.
And guard yourself from burning the nerve, if it is there, or a large vein: or if the fistula goes to the body of the bladder, or to the body of the intestines, then guard yourself from all these places.
And do not do this unless when the fistula is in a fleshy place: and you consider that it is not penetrating.
Then care for the place until it heals.
But if the place is sealed and materials are cut away from it, and it remains so for a long time, then you will know that it has now been completely healed.
And if materials are not cut away from it, then you will know that it is penetrating, or there is a corrupt opening deep within it, or as if it were one of those, the recollection of which will come in its place.
On the Manner of Cauterizing the Kidneys.
When pain occurs in the kidneys from cold, or from thick windiness, and the strength of the sick person is diminished because of it, then it is necessary to cauterize him above the navel, above the kidneys themselves, with a cautery over the whole kidney with a clauili cautery, of which mention was made previously.
And perhaps we should cauterize him a second time in the very navel. Therefore, three lines will come. Therefore, they will be better for relief.
Concerning the way of cauterizing the bladder.
When weakness and softening occur in the bladder from cold and dampness, until the sick person does not retain urine, then cauterize him in the lower part of the penis above the bladder, where the pubic hairs begin, and with a cautery from the right side of the penis, and another from the left: and let the length of that cauterization be according to the size of a knuckle; and cauterize him with a cautery below the back, or with two cauteries if he needs them; and let it be as mentioned previously, a clauili cautery.
Concerning the way of cauterizing the womb.
When cold and dampness occur in the womb, and because of it impregnation is prohibited, and her menses are corrupted, and their provocation is delayed, and pain occurs to her at their arrival, then it is necessary that she be cauterized with three cauteries around the navel, as we said in the cauterization of the bladder, and with a cautery above the hip below the back, or with two cauteries: and let the cautery be clauili.
Concerning the way of cauterizing the ankle in dislocation.
When the mucous humors are poured out to the Anchae bone and become the cause of its displacement from its place; and the sign thereof is that one leg is lengthened over the other when they are compared together; and the place of dislocation is found empty in it.
Therefore it is necessary that you cauterize the weak bone of the Anchae itself with a cautery like a circle; after you have marked with an encaustic in a circle around the bone, as it revolves; and so that the bone itself falls in the middle of the circle.
And if you do not have this cautery present, then cauterize it with three cauteries, with a large olive-wood cautery; and let the depth of the cautery be according to the thickness of the skin of the whole.
Then take care of it until it heals.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in sciatica.
When pain occurs in the Anchae bone, and its cause is cold and humors; and the weak person is cured with what we said in the division, and the cure does not take effect, and it becomes old; then it is necessary that you free the weak person from gross humors with fetid pills, or with artificial pills, and the like. Then cauterize him.
And the method of cautery in it is according to two methods: either cautery with burning medicines, or cautery with fire.
Cautery with fire is according to many methods.
One of which is that you cauterize over the Anchae bone itself with three triangular cauteries, according to this form. And make their depth good or bad. And let the space which is between each cautery be of the thickness of a finger; and let the cautery be olive-wood.
Sometimes, however, a cautery is made in the middle above the head of the wound itself. Therefore there are four cauteries.
And if you wish to cauterize with a circle, whose form precedes in the cauterization of a wide dislocation, with one: so that it is a circle containing the whole wound.
And burn the thickness of all the skin.
This is the method of cautery in sciatica, when the pain adheres to the wound itself and does not extend as far as the hip and leg.
But if it extends as far as the hip and leg, then cauterize it with two cauteries above the thigh, above the place to which the weakling points there, in which there is pain, and your cautery above the calf four fingers towards the woodland side a little: and let the cautery be sharp.
And let the depth of the cautery be according to the depth of the thickness of the skin.
But if the weakling points out that the pain extends as far as near the toes, then cauterize it there where he points with a point cautery, three, or four, or more, if he needs it.
And if he points out the pain to be below the knee towards the leg, then cautery it there with one sharp cautery.
And beware for yourself in all your cauteries, that you do not finish with the cautery so as to burn a nerve, or a large artery, and draw through it upon the weakling a bad harm, or contraction.
And I myself have now seen one and another, from those who have cauterized above the calf, and finished in the cautery, and the leg swelled up until a tumor reached the foot, and it was perforated all through, and the whole foot was corrupted: then there followed a rupture of the abdomen, and death after that.
If the pain is in both parts at the same time, cauterize both according to this method.
And certain wise men said that in the cauterization of a wide area, which cautery is of this mode. Make a cautery like a samarium iron, whose diameter is half a palm; and let it be at its opening according to the thickness of a fingernail, or a little less: and within that samarium let there be a third samarium.
And let the space that is between every samarium be by the quantity of a thumb joint; and let the samaria be open on two sides; and let the height of them be like a thumb joint, or two thumb joints; and make for them a handle from iron suitably fitted into the samaria.
Then ignite it in fire until it glows and projects sparks; then place it on a wide layer of pitch with the infirm person lying down on their healthy side. Therefore cauterize him with three circular cauteries in one spot.
Then let him go for three days. Afterwards apply a plaster with butter; and let the wound open for many days. Then care for it with ointment until it heals.
Says Albucasis, of this kind of cautery, O my son, we have used but little, because of the terror of its appearance; and therefore, because we found few who would endure it.
Nevertheless it is one of the good cauteries for him who suffers it, and finds with it its place.
This cautery however with medicines that harden is, for you to make two samaria having a perforated armilla, into which the bolt of its door descends from brass or iron, the length of a span; whose height shall be two thumb joints, or almost like them.
And there shall be a space which is between each quantity of the thickness of a finger, and they shall be open below and above; and let them contain themselves to each other, according to this form.
Then lay it upon the pillow, the weak one lying on his sound side. And press your hand upon the broad pillow greatly. Then pour between the two circles hot water, which has been heated with fire a little while, and hold it for the space of an hour; and let the weak one endure its biting and its burning, for he finds the bite like fire until the bite subsides.
Then raise your hand with the instrument and wipe away the hot water from the whole pillow with sweet water; then let it alone for three days.
And put butter upon it until the blackness of the burning is removed; and let it alone for several days, and let pus flow from it. For this is the final thing in healing.
Then care for it with ointments until it heals.
But if the pain extends as far as the hip or the leg: make for him a bath that contains water according to what you did for the pillow equally.
And this is the way of hot water: and I have already written it in the treatise on the rectification of medicines. Take alkali and quicklime, of each a half part; grind each one and put them in a new pot, whose lower part is perforated with one small hole according to the quantity that enters the radius; and put under the bottom of the pot another glazed pot; and pour over the alkali and lime sweet water, which shall submerge each by a finger; after which you shall press them with your hand with good compression; and let the pot stand until sharp water descends to the lower part of the glazed pot.
Then add all that water and pour it over other lime; and strain until it is renewed.
It will then indeed be very sharp and strong, which is used in many medical operations and for cauterizing the remaining limbs. Because it makes the operation of fire itself effective.
And among medicines are those with which anchas are cauterized, even as tesisie and mastic, and lime with soap, so that both may be mixed together.
And Galen indeed recounted the cure of a certain man from antiquity, who was cured of pain in the ancha and sciatic vein; and he praised it greatly. And he said that he needed no other treatment and that he was healed by one application only, until he recounted that he perhaps entered a bath carried in and came out of it already healed.
And it is to be taken from green seitaragi; and if green is not found, take the dry, fresh one; and knead it well with a little fat and place it on the ancha where there is pain, or the leg, or in the hip; and bind it up, and leave it for three hours, or for as long as the weak person feels the soothing of the burning. Then put him into a bath.
When therefore his body is warmed, place him on a couch. For the pain subsides and he heals.
And know that no one should use a cautery with these medicines except after evacuation of the body.
And Dioscorides who also said that goat dung when it is cauterized with the sciatic vein, strengthens it; and the cautery is made in this way. Take wool and soak it in old oil and place it on the deep spot which is between the big toe and the other toes and which is closer to the other toes.
Then take dry goat dung and inflame it in fire until it becomes charcoal.
Then place it upon wool and let it remain until it is extinguished. Then repeat that. Therefore do not cease to do that until sensation reaches the region of the neck by means of mediation and pain ceases.
And this method of cautery is called cautery vaccinum.
Concerning the cauterization of back pain.
Sometimes pain occurs in the back from many causes, either from a fall, or a blow, or excessive evacuation, and suchlike, from infusion of cold and humid matter; and cautery indeed does not apply except in this one kind which is caused by infusion of cold matter.
It is therefore necessary after evacuation of the sick person with fetid pills and suchlike, so that they are made upon the back, where there is pain, three lines according to the width of the almeidia itself, after making signs with a hot iron on each line five cauteries or more according to the quantity which comes from the tolerance of the strength of the sick person; and let the cauterization be done with a puncturing cautery.
And if you wish, cauterize with three cauteries or four with a medium-sized clavil cautery according to this form.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in incipient gibbosity.
Very often this illness happens to young infants.
And the sign of its inception in children is: a constriction occurs upon him in breathing at elevation and motion; and the youth in the last vertebra of the back and its nodes, which has already begun to protrude above the other vertebrae.
Therefore when you see that, and wish to do it, then cauterize it with a circular cautery according to this form.
And let him apply the cautery over every part of the vertebrae equally; and if you wish to cauterize around the vertebrae with a pointed cautery two lines, or three. And let the points be near to each other.
Then care for the place until it heals with what we have said.
And beware that you do not apply the cautery in a gibbosity which occurs in nerve spasm.
Concerning the manner of cauterizing in gout and pains of the joints.
When the pains of the joints are from cold humors which flow to any limb of the body, then when they happen in the feet, it is customary for physicians to name that gout properly.
Therefore, when gout of a cold cause is treated with methods of treatment and the pains are not removed, then the cautery removes them.
And it is, that you cauterize him after evacuation around the joint of the foot with many cauteries; and let the cautery be olive-wood.
And if it seems necessary to you to make points on the face of the foot, then do so with a pointed cautery. But if the pains ascend as far as the knees or other joints, and this often happens, then cauterize him over the whole knee with three or four cauteries on all sides with the same olive-wood cautery.
But if more of these cauteries are necessary for you, then cauterize him. And do not submerge your hand with the cautery, rather let it be about the thickness of the skin only.
But if the pains ascend to the knees and back: then administer what we have said from the cautery in its own chapter.
But if the pains are only in the hands then make points around the wrists as they turn like two lines.
If pain remains in the fingers, then prick them, a point over every knuckle and a point over the comb of the hand.
But if the pains rise after days to the elbows, or to the shoulders, then cauterize both on every side.
And do not withdraw the weak from a good regimen, from the taking of medicines. For if a good regimen is made and the phlegm is evacuated, he will be healed with the help of God along with this cautery.
On the manner of cauterizing in ruptures.
When a rupture occurs in the groin and the intestine or omentum descends to the testicle, and it is beginning nearby: then it is necessary that you advise the sick man to cease eating on his day of fasting. And let him use laxatives so that the dung descends from his belly.
Then let him sit between your hands upon his back and instruct him to hold his breath until it emerges or the omentum or intestine appears.
Then reduce it with your fingers and mark with hot wax beneath the rupture on the bone of the hip with a sign whose extremity is like half a circle toward the upper part of the body.
Then apply a cautery iron, which has this shape, until it becomes white and throws sparks. Then return the intestine or omentum to its cavity. Then let the attendant place his hand over the spot so that the intestine does not come out and you have already opened between the sick man's thighs and placed a cushion beneath him, and one servant over his thighs and another over his chest who holds his hands.
Then place the cautery upon the very mark, your hand with the cautery standing straight. And hold it until you reach a bone with it; or repeat it with another cautery if you have not reached a bone with the first one up to the bone.
And carefully observe from the exit of the intestine during your cauterization so that you do not burn it, and death or great harm comes through it upon the sick person.
And know that when you do not reach a bone with the cautery, your operation is of no effect.
And it is necessary that the cautery for infants be slender according to their measure.
Then care with the remaining ointments until it heals.
And let the sick person lie on their back for forty days until the wound is sealed.
And it is necessary that you give them nourishment for the length of their healing time, which soothes their stomach so that the intestine does not come out during straining and excretion.
Then when they wish to rise after forty days, then apply a bandage well made and let them wear it for another forty days.
And they should abstain from labor, and the fullness of food and drink, and loud voices.
For when they use this regimen, they are healed with complete healing.
And I will speak of the cure of ruptures with an incision in its own chapter.
But when ruptures occur in the rest of the belly and they are beginning, and you wish that they not be added to, then cauterize their rupture with a round cautery according to its size; and let that which is burned be from then on like a third of it. Then care for it as we have said, and it will not be added to.
And indeed some of the first have said: that a rupture should be cauterized with a triangular cautery, according to this form.
After it is marked with a cautery and a line is placed which is across the width on the upper side of the rupture, and another line below. And place your hand in the middle with a hot iron.
But the cautery first is easier and better.
On the way of cauterizing in pains because of a fall, or a blow.
Chapter XLVIII.
When it happens in certain limbs from a fall, or a blow pain: and that pain persists for a long time, and healing does not occur in it with medicine: then it is necessary that it be cauterized with a point cautery.
And let the cautery of every limb be a cautery according to its size, and its suitability, and its weakness, and its power, and the location of the twist, and the pain from it.
Therefore if it is healed from the first cautery, it is well. If not: then repeat the cautery upon it.
For it is customary for these pains to change from one limb to that which is close to it. Therefore it is necessary that you follow them with a cautery until the weak one is healed.
On the way of cauterizing in leprosy.
Those with leprosy are sometimes greatly helped by cauterization. And especially the kind of leprosy which is caused by the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy: therefore when you wish to cauterize it consider.
Therefore if the leprosy is beginning and you have treated it with what we said in the division and it does not descend nor stand still: and you fear for the sick person that corruption may spread over their whole complexion: then cauterize them on the head with five cauteries: one in the middle of the head known, and a second below it towards the forehead at the end of the hair, and two above the two horns, and one behind above the nape of the neck.
And finally impress your hand with a cautery for a short time, until it makes a slight impression on the mouth, and the barks are loosened from it: so that the expiration of gross vapors is relieved from it, and also cauterize the spleen itself with a cautery, as previously mentioned.
But if leprosy is already spread over the sick person and appears manifestly, then it is necessary to cauterize with these cauteries, which we mentioned in the head, and with a cautery on the extremity of the nose, and two cauteries on the two maxillas, and two cauteries on the vertebrae of the neck, and six on the vertebrae of the back, and one large one on the alhosos at the base of the tail and one above it, on itself in the almeidati: and two on the anchas: namely, on every ancha with one, and two on the knees: one on every knee, and two on the shoulders, and two on the elbows, and two on the tenderness of his chest. And cauterize him on every joint, from the joints of the fingers of his hands and feet: and cauterize on every heel of his feet, and the focilia of his hands.
And be careful of the nerves that are on the last part of the heel so as not to burn them.
And sometimes it is cauterized with a cautery on the breastbone, and another on the stomach bone, and another on the liver.
And know that the more you add a cautery, the more benefit there is, and the more it brings together.
And know that the sick person does not find pain in the cautery as healthy people do: because his body is already stunned.
And it is necessary that the cauteries be of size and smallness according to the limbs and joints: as previously mentioned from the types of instruments.
Then take care of the cautery with flour of herbs and honey, and other care, until it is healed.
On the manner of cauterizing in a state of stupor.
When a limb is in a state of stupor and it is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, and it does not heal, then cauterize the stupefied limb with cauteries, according to the size or smallness of the limb.
And let your cautery be thrust into the thickness of the skin a little. Then care for it with ointment until it heals.
And sometimes it is cauterized for a certain stupor which happens to the hand and foot, in the vertebrae of the back near the exit of the nerves which move that limb; and the stupor is removed.
But let no one presume upon this unless he is wise in the anatomy of the members and the exit of the nerves that move the body.
Head LI.
When an albara becomes old and nothing from the arts of medicine takes effect in it, then cauterize over it with a deep cautery for a little while, according to the amount of thickness of the skin, until the whiteness is removed and its color is changed.
Then care for it with flour of herbs and lentils with rose oil and leaves of arnoglossa and dove's blood and swallow's blood: let there be one part of each; mix all these things together and spread them upon a cloth and apply them to the place until it heals.
On the manner of cauterizing in Cancer.
When a cancer is beginning and you wish to stop it, then cauterize it with a circular cautery all around it, as if it were revolving.
Wise men, however, have said that it should be cauterized with the last cautery in the middle.
But it does not seem right to me; for I fear that it might be injured; and I have already seen that happen many times.
And it is better that it be cauterized around it with a circle, as we said, or with many cauteries.
Concerning the method of cauterizing an adubelati.
When someone has an adubelati and it is delayed in maturation, either because of excessive discharge making it so, or because of the weakness due to age, when they are elderly and have little blood, or because of time and the desire to hasten the maturation of the adubelati, then cauterize around it with many small cauteries by puncturing. Then let it alone. For it will hasten to maturity itself.
But if you wish to perforate it with a cautery, then use a fire-cautery which has this shape.
And place it in the middle of the adubelati until it penetrates the skin, and let the cautery be weak following this one so that the course of pus is relieved.
Then care for it until it heals.
Concerning the method of cauterizing a malignant corrosive.
Chapter Fifty-Four.
A corrosive is nothing but a corruption in a limb that wanders and eats it away, just as fire consumes dry wood.
Therefore if you see a corrosive in a place that can tolerate a fire cautery then use many fire cauteries, small and large, according to what suits the place where the corrosive is.
Then cauterize it from every side until you eradicate the entire corruption and nothing remains of it at all.
Then let it alone for three days and place powdered sulfur mixed with oil on the cauterized areas until all the scabs and all corruption are eradicated.
Then care for it with ointments that generate flesh.
So if you see that after three days healthy flesh is born, in which there is no corruption, it is good.
And if not: then repeat the cautery over that which remained from the corrupt places.
And it is sometimes treated with a sharp medicine when corroding. For it arises in place of the cautery.
But cautery with fire is of quicker healing; and I have indeed already said cauterization of it with a sharp medicine in the division: therefore take that there when it is needed.
On the way of cauterizing warts and moles.
Chapter Fifty-five.
Very often this ailment occurs in the lower parts of the feet; and it is a thick, filtered thing which harms the foot.
And cautery indeed in them is according to two methods: cautery with fire and cautery with hot water.
But as much as with fire, that the cautery be concave like a vulture's quill; which should be made of iron according to the quantity it contains of warts from every part and have subtle edges.
Then place it ignited upon the wart. Then revolve your hand with the cautery around the wart until the cautery reaches the depth of the wart; and leave it for three days until it begins to discharge pus. Then apply a plaster with wild mallows crushed with salt; and leave the plaster upon it at night. For it will be eradicated from its roots.
Then care for the place with an ointment that generates flesh until it is healed.
But if they are unconverted and very often occur on the surface of the body, especially on the hands and feet; then administer to them cautery with hot water; and it is that you take a cannula from bronze, or iron, or from a vulture's quill; and place it upon the wart, or althelul.
